However, during his second premiership between 1880 and 1885 he could not resist the colonial lobby in his cabinet, and thus did not execute his electoral promise to disengage from Egypt. Although Gladstone was personally opposed to imperialism, the <a href="/wiki/Class_conflict" title="Class conflict">social tensions</a> caused by the Long Depression pushed him to favour <a href="/wiki/Jingoism" title="Jingoism">jingoism</a>: the imperialists had become the "parasites of patriotism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radical_Party_(France)" title="Radical Party (France)">Radical</a> politician <a href="/wiki/Georges_Clemenceau" title="Georges Clemenceau">Georges Clemenceau</a> was adamantly opposed to it: he thought colonization was a diversion from the "blue line of the <a href="/wiki/Vosges" title="Vosges">Vosges</a>" mountains, that is <a href="/wiki/Revanchism" title="Revanchism">revanchism</a> and the patriotic urge to reclaim the <a href="/wiki/Alsace%E2%80%93Lorraine" title="Alsace–Lorraine">Alsace-Lorraine</a> region which had been annexed by the German Empire with the 1871 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Frankfurt_(1871)" title="Treaty of Frankfurt (1871)">Treaty of Frankfurt</a>. Clemenceau actually made <a href="/wiki/Jules_Ferry" title="Jules Ferry">Jules Ferry</a>'s cabinet fall after the 1885 <a href="/wiki/Sino-French_War" title="Sino-French War">Tonkin disaster</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Hannah_Arendt" title="Hannah Arendt">Hannah Arendt</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Origins_of_Totalitarianism" title="The Origins of Totalitarianism">The Origins of Totalitarianism</a></i> (1951), this expansion of national sovereignty on overseas territories contradicted the unity of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation state</a> which provided citizenship to its population. Thus, a tension between the <a href="/wiki/Moral_universalism" title="Moral universalism">universalist</a> will to respect human rights of the colonized people, as they may be considered as "citizens" of the nation state, and the imperialist drive to cynically <a href="/wiki/Exploitation_of_labour" title="Exploitation of labour">exploit populations</a> deemed inferior began to surface. Some, in colonizing countries, opposed what they saw as unnecessary evils of the colonial administration when left to itself; as described in <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Conrad" title="Joseph Conrad">Joseph Conrad</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Darkness" title="Heart of Darkness">Heart of Darkness</a></i> (1899)—published around the same time as <a href="/wiki/Rudyard_Kipling" title="Rudyard Kipling">Kipling</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_White_Man%27s_Burden" title="The White Man's Burden">The White Man's Burden</a></i>—or in <a href="/wiki/Louis-Ferdinand_C%C3%A9line" title="Louis-Ferdinand Céline">Louis-Ferdinand Céline</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_to_the_End_of_the_Night" title="Journey to the End of the Night">Journey to the End of the Night</a></i> (1932).
</p><p>Colonial lobbies emerged to legitimise the Scramble for Africa and other expensive overseas adventures. In Germany, France, and Britain, the middle class often sought strong overseas policies to ensure the market's growth. Even in lesser powers, voices like <a href="/wiki/Enrico_Corradini" title="Enrico Corradini">Enrico Corradini</a> claimed a "place in the sun" for so-called "proletarian nations", bolstering nationalism and militarism in an early prototype of fascism.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_propaganda_and_jingoism">Colonial propaganda and jingoism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Colonial propaganda and jingoism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A plethora of colonialist propaganda pamphlets, ideas, and imagery played on the colonial powers' psychology of popular jingoism and proud nationalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> A hallmark of the French colonial project in the late 19th century and early 20th century was the <a href="/wiki/Civilizing_mission" title="Civilizing mission">civilizing mission</a> (<i>mission civilisatrice</i>), the principle that it was Europe's duty to bring civilisation to benighted peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> As such, colonial officials undertook a policy of Franco-Europeanisation in French colonies, most notably <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Madagascar" title="French Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. During the 19th century, French citizenship along with the right to elect a deputy to the French Chamber of Deputies was granted to the four old colonies of Guadeloupe, Martinique, Guyanne and Réunion as well as to the residents of the "<a href="/wiki/Four_Communes" title="Four Communes">Four Communes</a>" in Senegal. In most cases, the elected deputies were white Frenchmen, although there were some black deputies, such as the Senegalese <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Diagne" title="Blaise Diagne">Blaise Diagne</a>, who was elected in 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Segalla_2009_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Segalla_2009-80">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_exhibitions">Colonial exhibitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Colonial exhibitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2186" data-file-width="2962" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg/220px-Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg/330px-Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg/440px-Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dellepiane-exposition-nationale-coloniale-1906.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Poster for the 1906 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Exhibition" title="Colonial Exhibition">Colonial Exhibition</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marseilles" title="Marseilles">Marseilles</a> (France)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Affiche_exposition_coloniale_Tervuren.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="235" decoding="async" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Affiche_exposition_coloniale_Tervuren.jpg/170px-Affiche_exposition_coloniale_Tervuren.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/aa/Affiche_exposition_coloniale_Tervuren.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Affiche_exposition_coloniale_Tervuren.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Poster for the 1897 <a href="/wiki/Brussels_International_Exposition_(1897)" title="Brussels International Exposition (1897)">Brussels International Exposition</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>By the end of World War I the colonial empires had become very popular almost everywhere in Europe: <a href="/wiki/Public_opinion" title="Public opinion">public opinion</a> had been convinced of the needs of a colonial empire, although most of the metropolitans would never see a piece of it. <a href="/wiki/Colonial_exhibition" title="Colonial exhibition">Colonial exhibitions</a> were instrumental in this change of popular mentalities brought about by the colonial propaganda, supported by the colonial lobby and by various scientists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Thus, conquests of territories were inevitably followed by public displays of the indigenous people for scientific and leisure purposes.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Carl_Hagenbeck" title="Carl Hagenbeck">Carl Hagenbeck</a>, a German merchant in wild animals and a future entrepreneur of most Europeans zoos, decided in 1874 to exhibit <a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A1mi" title="Sámi">Sami people</a> as "purely natural" populations. In 1876, he sent one of his collaborators to the newly conquered Egyptian Sudan to bring back some wild beasts and <a href="/wiki/Nubians" title="Nubians">Nubians</a>. Presented in Paris, London, and Berlin these Nubians were very successful. Such "<a href="/wiki/Human_zoo" title="Human zoo">human zoos</a>" could be found in Hamburg, Antwerp, Barcelona, London, Milan, New York City, Paris, etc., with 200,000 to 300,000 visitors attending each exhibition. <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_people" title="Tuareg people">Tuaregs</a> were exhibited after the French conquest of <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">Timbuktu</a> (visited by <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Cailli%C3%A9" title="René Caillié">René Caillié</a>, disguised as a Muslim, in 1828, thereby winning the prize offered by the French <i>Société de Géographie</i>); <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">Malagasy</a> after the occupation of Madagascar; <a href="/wiki/Dahomey_Amazons" title="Dahomey Amazons">Amazons</a> of <a href="/wiki/Abomey" title="Abomey">Abomey</a> after <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9hanzin" title="Béhanzin">Behanzin</a>'s mediatic defeat against the French in 1894. Not used to the climatic conditions, some of the indigenous died from exposure, such as some <a href="/wiki/Kalina_people" title="Kalina people">Galibis</a> in Paris in 1892.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Geoffroy de Saint-Hilaire, director of the <a href="/wiki/Jardin_d%27Acclimatation" title="Jardin d'Acclimatation">Jardin d'Acclimatation</a>, decided in 1877 to organise two "ethnological spectacles", presenting Nubians and <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>. Ticket sales at the Jardin d'Acclimatation doubled, with a million paying entrances that year, a huge success for these times. Between 1877 and 1912, approximately thirty "ethnological exhibitions" were presented at the zoo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> "Negro villages" were presented in Paris' <a href="/wiki/Exposition_Universelle_(1878)" title="Exposition Universelle (1878)">1878 World's Fair</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Exposition_Universelle_(1900)" title="Exposition Universelle (1900)">1900 World's Fair</a> presented the famous <a href="/wiki/Diorama" title="Diorama">diorama</a> "living" in Madagascar, while the Colonial Exhibitions in Marseilles (1906 and 1922) and in Paris (1907 and 1931)displayed human beings in cages, often nudes or quasi-nudes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Nomadic "Senegalese villages" were also created, thus displaying the power of the colonial empire to all the population.
</p><p>In the U.S., <a href="/wiki/Madison_Grant" title="Madison Grant">Madison Grant</a>, head of the New York Zoological Society, exposed <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">Pygmy</a> <a href="/wiki/Ota_Benga" title="Ota Benga">Ota Benga</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Zoo" title="Bronx Zoo">Bronx Zoo</a> alongside the apes and others in 1906. At the behest of Grant, a <a href="/wiki/Scientific_racism" title="Scientific racism">scientific racist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eugenics" title="Eugenics">eugenicist</a>, zoo director <a href="/wiki/William_Temple_Hornaday" title="William Temple Hornaday">William Temple Hornaday</a> placed Ota Benga in a cage with an orangutan and labeled him "The <a href="/wiki/Missing_link_(human_evolution)" title="Missing link (human evolution)">Missing Link</a>" in an attempt to illustrate <a href="/wiki/Darwinism" title="Darwinism">Darwinism</a>, and in particular that Africans like Ota Benga are closer to apes than were Europeans. Other colonial exhibitions included the 1924 <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Exhibition" title="British Empire Exhibition">British Empire Exhibition</a> and the 1931 Paris "Exposition coloniale".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countering_disease">Countering disease</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Countering disease">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From the beginning of the 20th century, the elimination or control of disease in tropical countries became a driving force for all colonial powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a> epidemic in Africa was arrested through mobile teams systematically screening millions of people at risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In the 1880s cattle brought from British Asia to feed Italian soldiers invading Eritrea turned out to be infected with a disease called <a href="/wiki/Rinderpest" title="Rinderpest">rinderpest</a>. It continues to infect 90% of Africa's cattle. Decimation of native herds severely damaged local livelihoods, forcing people to labor for their colonizers.
</p><p>In the 20th century, Africa saw the biggest increase in its population because of lessening of the <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality rate</a> in many countries through peace, famine relief, <a href="/wiki/Medicine#Modern" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, and above all, the end or decline of the slave trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Africa's population has grown from 120 million in 1900<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> to over 1 billion today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Slavery_abolition">Slavery abolition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Slavery abolition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa#Abolition" title="Slavery in Africa">Slavery in Africa § Abolition</a></div>
<p>The continuing <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism" title="Abolitionism">anti-slavery movement</a> in Western Europe became a reason and an excuse for the conquest and colonization of Africa. It was the central theme of the <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Anti-Slavery_Conference_1889%E2%80%9390" title="Brussels Anti-Slavery Conference 1889–90">Brussels Anti-Slavery Conference 1889–90</a>. During the Scramble for Africa, an early but secondary focus of all colonial regimes was the suppression of slavery and the slave trade. In French West Africa, following conquest and abolition by the French, over one million slaves fled from their masters to earlier homes between 1906 and 1911. In Madagascar, the French abolished slavery in 1896, and approximately 500,000 slaves were freed. Slavery was abolished in the French controlled Sahel by 1911. Independent nations attempting to westernize or impress Europe sometimes cultivated an image of slavery suppression. In response to European pressure, the <a href="/wiki/Sokoto_Caliphate" title="Sokoto Caliphate">Sokoto Caliphate</a> abolished slavery in 1900, and Ethiopia officially abolished slavery in 1932. Colonial powers were mostly successful in abolishing slavery, though slavery remained active in Africa, even though it has gradually moved to a wage economy. Slavery was never fully eradicated in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manning-1990_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Manning-1990-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lovejoy,_Paul_E._2012_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lovejoy,_Paul_E._2012-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_(Cameroon).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="473" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Victoria_%28Cameroon%29.jpg/220px-Victoria_%28Cameroon%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Victoria_%28Cameroon%29.jpg/330px-Victoria_%28Cameroon%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Victoria_%28Cameroon%29.jpg/440px-Victoria_%28Cameroon%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Victoria_(Cameroon).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Cameroon" title="German Cameroon">German Cameroon</a>, painting by <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Hellgrewe" title="Rudolf Hellgrewe">R. Hellgrewe</a>, 1908</div></div></div>
<p>During the New Imperialism period, by the end of the 19th century, Europe added almost 9,000,000 square miles (23,000,000 km<sup>2</sup>) – one-fifth of the land area of the globe – to its overseas colonial possessions. Europe's formal holdings included the entire African continent except Ethiopia, Liberia, and <a href="/wiki/Saguia_el-Hamra" title="Saguia el-Hamra">Saguia el-Hamra</a>, the latter of which was eventually integrated into <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Sahara" title="Spanish Sahara">Spanish Sahara</a>. Between 1885 and 1914, Britain took nearly 30% of Africa's population under its control; 15% for France, 11% for Portugal, 9% for Germany, 7% for Belgium and 1% for Italy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Nigeria alone contributed 15 million subjects, more than in the whole of French West Africa or the entire German colonial empire. In terms of surface area occupied, the French were the marginal leaders, but much of their territory consisted of the sparsely populated Sahara.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>Political imperialism followed the economic expansion, with the "colonial lobbies" bolstering chauvinism and jingoism at each crisis in order to legitimise the colonial enterprise. The tensions between the imperial powers led to a succession of crises, which exploded in August 1914, when previous rivalries and alliances created a domino situation that drew the major European nations into World War I.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="African_colonies_listed_by_colonising_power">African colonies listed by colonising power</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: African colonies listed by colonising power">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leopold_II_Statue_at_Place_du_Tr%C3%B4ne_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Equestrian statue of <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II_of_Belgium" title="Leopold II of Belgium">Leopold II of Belgium</a>, the Sovereign of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a> from 1885 to 1908, Regent Place in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, Belgium</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Belgium">Belgium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Belgium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Congo_Free_State" title="Congo Free State">Congo Free State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Congo" title="Belgian Congo">Belgian Congo</a> (today's the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ruanda-Urundi" title="Ruanda-Urundi">Ruanda-Urundi</a> (comprising modern <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, 1922–62)</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/French_Africa" title="French Africa">French Africa</a></div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Kamerun" title="German Kamerun">German Kamerun</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, 1884–1916)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/German_East_Africa" title="German East Africa">German East Africa</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> and most of <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, 1885–1919)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_South-West_Africa" title="German South-West Africa">German South-West Africa</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>, 1884–1915)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Togoland" title="German Togoland">German Togoland</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a> and eastern part of <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, 1884–1914)</li></ul>
<p>After the First World War, Germany's possessions were partitioned among Britain (which took a sliver of western Cameroon, Tanzania, western Togo, and Namibia), France (which took most of Cameroon and eastern Togo) and Belgium (which took Rwanda and Burundi).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika,_Massana_(Massawa,_Massaua)-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4292" data-file-width="4341" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika%2C_Massana_%28Massawa%2C_Massaua%29-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg/220px-CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika%2C_Massana_%28Massawa%2C_Massaua%29-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika%2C_Massana_%28Massawa%2C_Massaua%29-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg/330px-CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika%2C_Massana_%28Massawa%2C_Massaua%29-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika%2C_Massana_%28Massawa%2C_Massaua%29-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg/440px-CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika%2C_Massana_%28Massawa%2C_Massaua%29-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CH-NB_-_Italienisch-Ostafrika,_Massana_(Massawa,_Massaua)-_Hafen_-_Annemarie_Schwarzenbach_-_SLA-Schwarzenbach-A-5-23-129.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Italian settlers in <a href="/wiki/Massawa" title="Massawa">Massawa</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Italian_Eritrea" title="Italian Eritrea">Italian Eritrea</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Somalia" title="Italian Somalia">Italian Somalia</a>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Oltre_Giuba" title="Oltre Giuba">Oltre Giuba</a></i> <span style="font-size:85%;">(annexed into Italian Somalia in 1925)</span></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Italian_colonization_of_Libya" title="Italian colonization of Libya">Libya</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Italian_Tripolitania" title="Italian Tripolitania">Italian Tripolitania</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Italian_Cyrenaica" title="Italian Cyrenaica">Italian Cyrenaica</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Italian_Libya" title="Italian Libya">Italian Libya</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(from the unification of Tripolitania and Cyrenaica in 1934)</span></li></ul></li></ul>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Ethiopia" title="Italian Ethiopia">Italian Ethiopia</a> formed together with Italian Eritrea and Italian Somaliland the <a href="/wiki/Italian_East_Africa" title="Italian East Africa">Italian East Africa</a> (A.O.I., "Africa Orientale Italiana", also defined by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy#Fascist_regime_(1922–1943)" title="Kingdom of Italy">fascist government</a> as <i>L'Impero</i>).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Combat_de_marracuene.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="639" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Combat_de_marracuene.jpg/220px-Combat_de_marracuene.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Combat_de_marracuene.jpg/330px-Combat_de_marracuene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Combat_de_marracuene.jpg/440px-Combat_de_marracuene.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Combat_de_marracuene.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marracuene" title="Marracuene">Marracuene</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mozambique" title="Portuguese Mozambique">Portuguese Mozambique</a> was the site of a decisive battle between Portuguese and <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Empire" title="Gaza Empire">Gaza</a> king <a href="/wiki/Gungunhana" title="Gungunhana">Gungunhana</a> in 1895</div></div></div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Historiography_of_the_British_Empire" title="Historiography of the British Empire">Historiography of the British Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1899railroad_salisbury.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="225" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/1899railroad_salisbury.jpg/220px-1899railroad_salisbury.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/1899railroad_salisbury.jpg/330px-1899railroad_salisbury.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/1899railroad_salisbury.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1899railroad_salisbury.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opening of the railway in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rhodesia" title="Southern Rhodesia">Rhodesia</a>, 1899</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="377" data-file-width="618" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg/220px-Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg/330px-Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg/440px-Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prempeh-124-palaver-and-submission.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fourth_Anglo-Ashanti_War" title="Fourth Anglo-Ashanti War">Fourth Anglo-Ashanti War</a> in 1896, the British proclaimed a protectorate over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashanti_Kingdom" title="Ashanti Kingdom">Ashanti Kingdom</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The British were primarily interested in maintaining secure communication lines to <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, which led to initial interest in <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. Once these two areas were secure, it was the intent of British colonialists such as <a href="/wiki/Cecil_Rhodes" title="Cecil Rhodes">Cecil Rhodes</a> to establish a Cape-Cairo railway and to exploit mineral and agricultural resources. Control of the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> was viewed as a strategic and commercial advantage.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_states">Independent states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Independent states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Liberia was the only nation in Africa that was regarded as a colony and a protectorate of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Liberia was founded, colonised, established and controlled by the <a href="/wiki/American_Colonization_Society" title="American Colonization Society">American Colonization Society</a>, a private organisation established in order to relocate freed <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African American</a> and Caribbean slaves from the United States and the Caribbean islands in 1822.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Liberia declared its independence from the American Colonization Society on July 26, 1847.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Liberia is Africa's oldest republic and the second-oldest black republic in the world (after Haiti). Liberia maintained its independence during the period as it was viewed by European powers as either a colony<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> or protectorate of the United States.
</p><p>The same powers assumed Ethiopia to be a protectorate of Italy although the country had never accepted this, and its independence from Italy was recognized after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Adwa" title="Battle of Adwa">Battle of Adwa</a> which resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Addis_Ababa" title="Treaty of Addis Ababa">Treaty of Addis Ababa</a> in 1896.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> With the exception of Italian occupation between 1936 and 1941 by <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>'s military forces, Ethiopia is Africa's oldest independent nation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Connections_to_modern-day_events">Connections to modern-day events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Connections to modern-day events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa" title="Decolonisation of Africa">Decolonisation of Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neocolonialism" title="Neocolonialism">Neocolonialism</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="762" data-file-width="510" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png/170px-Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png/255px-Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png/340px-Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sudan_Map_Oelgas.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oil and gas concessions in the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> – 2004</div></div></div>
<p>Anti-neoliberal scholars connect the old scramble to a new scramble for Africa, coinciding with the emergence of an "Afro-neoliberal" capitalist movement in postcolonial Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> When African nations began to gain independence after World War II, their postcolonial economic structures remained undiversified and linear. In most cases, the bulk of a nation's economy relied on <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crops</a> or <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>. These scholars claim that the decolonisation process kept independent African nations at the mercy of colonial powers by structurally dependent economic relations. They also claim that structural adjustment programs led to the privatization and liberalization of many African political and economic systems, forcefully pushing Africa into the global capitalist market, and that these factors led to development under Western ideological systems of economics and politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Petrostates">Petrostates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Petrostates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the era of <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>, several African countries have emerged as <a href="/wiki/Petrostate" title="Petrostate">petrostates</a> (for example Angola, Cameroon, Nigeria, and Sudan). These are nations with an economic and political partnership between transnational oil companies and the ruling elite class in oil-rich African nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Numerous countries have entered into a neo-imperial relationship with Africa during this time period. Mary Gilmartin notes that “material and symbolic appropriation of space [is] central to imperial expansion and control”; nations in the globalization era who invest in controlling land internationally are engaging in neocolonialism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Chinese (and other Asian countries) state oil companies have entered Africa's highly competitive oil sector. <a href="/wiki/China_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="China National Petroleum Corporation">China National Petroleum Corporation</a> purchased 40% of Greater Nile Petroleum Operating Company. Furthermore, the Sudan exports 50–60% of its domestically produced oil to China, making up 7% of China's imports. China has also been purchasing equity shares in African oil fields, invested in industry related infrastructure development and acquired continental oil concessions throughout Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Scramble_for_Africa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<ul>
<li><span><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/31px-P_history.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/47px-P_history.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/P_history.svg/62px-P_history.svg.png 2x" width="31"/></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:History" title="Portal:History">History portal</a></span></li>
<li><span><img alt="map" class="noviewer" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="28" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/28px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/42px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/56px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" width="28"/></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Africa" title="Portal:Africa">Africa portal</a></span></li></ul></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Analysis_of_Western_European_colonialism_and_colonization" title="Analysis of Western European colonialism and colonization">Analysis of Western European colonialism and colonization</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chronology_of_Western_colonialism" title="Chronology of Western colonialism">Chronology of Western colonialism</a></li>
